<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">Passive UHF radio frequency identification (RFID) tag is proposed for integration into aluminum blister medicine package. To fit the very limited space left on aluminum foil and inevitable errors in hot-press fabrication, an antenna of multiple-fold slot is optimized in terms of normalized tag performance index and Latin hypercube sampling model of fabrication errors in hot-press. It is shown that the antenna of one-fold slot provides the largest read range, while the antenna of zero-fold slot (single rectangular slot) provides the best tolerance to fabrication errors. Prototypes of UHF tag with zero-fold and one-fold slot antenna are fabricated and tested, respectively. For 50 tags with zero-fold slot antenna, an average maximum read range of approximately 1.18 m is measured by using a UHF reader of 4 W EIRP at 915 MHz. For 50 tags with one-fold slot antenna, an average maximum read range of 3.19 m is measured.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID) technology is expected to play a more important role in medicine management and drug safety <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. Nowadays, some RFID-based medical applications, including drug delivery tracking <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>; distribution of pharmaceutical drugs <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>; blood collection, processing, distribution, and transfusion <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>; and animal oral drug experiment control <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, have been reported.</p><p>Many kinds of commercial RFID tags can be considered for medicine identification if the RFID tag is attached to medicine paper package <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. To attach an RFID tag directly to aluminum blister medicine package, anti-metal RFID tag can be considered. Unfortunately, it is hard for these anti-metal tags to fit the medicine blister package due to either the relatively large tag size or complex tag structures for mounting <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>.</p><p>RFID tags with slot antenna carved on aluminum foil seem quite suitable for medicine blister package. However, the slot should be specially designed for hot-pressed aluminum blister. In addition to the very limited space left on medicine blister for carving the slot antenna, there is another major design challenge, i.e., effects of fabrication errors in hot-press fabrication of medicine aluminum blister should be included at the design stage. Otherwise, a well-designed high performance of slot antenna for RFID tag cannot be maintained in hot-press fabrication.</p><p>To include errors of hot-press fabrication in antenna slot design, a comprehensive factor must be defined for tag performance evaluation. Statistical methods can be applied to building a model for fabrication errors analysis. Latin hypercube sampling <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> is a statistical method for generating a sample of plausible collections of parameter values from a multidimensional distribution. For design of slot antenna with quite a lot of geometry parameters, the Latin hypercube sampling method can be very helpful.</p><p>In this letter, we report the design of passive UHF RFID tags with slot antenna of enough tolerance to hot-press fabrication errors that is suitable for integration into aluminum blister medicine package. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, geometry and deployment of tag antenna of multiple-fold slot are proposed. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>, analysis flow of fabrication errors is introduced to finding the satisfactory fold number for maximum read range and best tolerance to fabrication errors among slots of different folds. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>, prototype tags with zero-fold slot and one-fold slot are fabricated and tested by using an Alien ALR 9900 reader (of 4 W EIRP) to verify the design.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Tag Deployment and Slot Structure</h2></div><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Design area on blister package.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7286772/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
Although different blister medicine packages may have different dimensions, there is always a space left for incused production date and other information, as shown by the design area in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. General dimensions of the incused space are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm L}4 = 8~\hbox{mm}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-4"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">4</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">8</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">{\rm L}4 = 8~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. We will restrict our RFID slot antenna within this space. The RFID chip may be installed across the slot on aluminum foil blister package.<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Multifold Meander Slot Antenna</h3><p>With no loss of generality, a relatively small dimension of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm L}1 \times {\rm L}2 = 46 \times 92~\hbox{mm}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-13" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-21"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-24" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">46</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-26" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-27" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">92</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-31"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-33"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-34"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">{\rm L}1 \times {\rm L}2 = 46 \times 92~\hbox{mm}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm L}3 = 40~\hbox{mm}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-36" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-37"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-38"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-40" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-42" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-43" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">40</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-46"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-47" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">{\rm L}3 = 40~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be considered for demonstration. Hence, a design space of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm L}3 \times {\rm L}4 = 40 \times 8~\hbox{mm}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-48" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-49"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-50"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-51"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-52" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-53" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-54" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-55" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-56"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-57" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-58" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">4</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-59" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-60" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">40</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-61" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-62" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">8</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-63" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-64"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-65"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-66"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-67" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-68"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-69"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-70" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">{\rm L}3 \times {\rm L}4 = 40 \times 8~\hbox{mm}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is left for slot antenna on aluminum foil blister.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Antenna with (a) symmetrical multifold slot and (b) zero-fold slot.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7286772/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
For such a restricted design space, meander slot antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2a">[12]</a> is a good candidate. An <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-71" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-72"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-73" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-fold slot is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a>. In addition to slot parameters defined in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a>, fold number <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-74" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-75"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-76" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is also a major indicator.<p></p><p>For the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-77" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-78"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-79" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-fold slot in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(a)</a>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-80" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-81"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-82" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">a</script></tex-math></inline-formula> characterizes position of slot antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">b</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-83" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-84"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-85" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">b</script></tex-math></inline-formula> defines length of the folded slot, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-86" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-87"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-88" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">s</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">s</script></tex-math></inline-formula> defines half-interval between the two symmetrical slot arms, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">w</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-89" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-90"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-91" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">w</script></tex-math></inline-formula> defines width of slot, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-92" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-93"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-94" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> defines width of metal strip between two neighboring slots, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">c</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-95" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-96"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-97" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">c</script></tex-math></inline-formula> defines width of gap for chip mounting. To simplify the antenna structure, all <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-98" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-99"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-100" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> parameters are set to be the same, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">c</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-101" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-102"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-103" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">c</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is set to be 1 mm, which is suitable for mounting RFID chip such as Impinj Monza-4 chip. It should be noted that zero-fold slot antenna has two symmetrical rectangular slots, which means <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-104" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-105"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-106" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-107" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-108" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">d = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2(b)</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Tag Performance Analysis</h3><p>For a passive UHF RFID tag of chip impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Z_c} = {R_c} + j{X_c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-109" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-110"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-111"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-112"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-113"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-114" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-115" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-116" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-117" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-118"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-119"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-120" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-121" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-122" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-123" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-124"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-125"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.84em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-127" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">X<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-size: 70.7%; A larger value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-393" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-401" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span style="display: inline-block; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.607em 1001.75em 3.967em -999.997em); top: -4.622em; left: 1.024em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; font-family: MathJax_Main; top: -4.021em; left: -0.057em;">−<span style="display: inline-block; Fabrication Errors Analysis</h3><p>For hot-pressed RFID slot antenna on aluminum blister, effects of fabrication errors should be considered in optimization design of slot antenna.</p><p>To model fabrication errors of the hot-press process for aluminum blister, statistical sampling method can be applied. In hot-press process, errors are majorly due to slot dimension errors, which can be considered to conform to Gaussian distribution with a standard deviation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-403" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-404"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-405" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">σ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Deviation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma = \break 0.2~</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-406" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-407"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-408" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">σ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-409" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-410" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.2</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-411" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">\sigma = \break 0.2~</script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2c">[14]</a> ensures dimension errors within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\pm }0.6~\hbox{mm}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-412" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-413"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-414"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-415"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-416" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">±</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-417" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.6</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-418" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-419"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-420"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-421" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">{\pm }0.6~\hbox{mm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> based on three-sigma rule or empirical rule <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2c">[11]</a>, which is reasonable for practical hot-press of aluminum blister. Since there are five key parameters, viz., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a, d, w, b</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-422" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-423"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-424" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-425" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-426" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.183em;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-427" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-428" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.183em;">w</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-429" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-430" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.183em;">b</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">a, d, w, b</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-431" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-432"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-433" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">s</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">s</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, defining an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-434" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-435"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-436" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-fold slot and different parameters have different effects on RFID tag performance, a comprehensive factor must be defined to include errors from all the key geometry parameters.</p><p>Latin hypercube sampling <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2c">[11]</a> is a compromise procedure that may incorporate many of the desirable features of random sampling and stratified sampling, and may produce more stable analysis outcomes than random sampling. To include all random errors of five key parameters defining an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-437" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-438"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-439" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">m</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-fold slot antenna, Latin hypercube sampling is an ideal technique to form a comprehensive factor to characterize hot-press fabrication errors.</p><p>With Latin hypercube sampling, a comprehensive factor to evaluate influence of random fabrication errors can be defined by normalized root mean square error (NRMSE) as <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2c">[15]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn3" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE = {{\sqrt {{{\sum\nolimits_{t = 1}^n {{{({\mathtilde{y}_t} - y)}^2}} } \over n}} } \over {{y_{t\_\max}} - {y_{t\_\min}}}} \times 100\% \eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-37">NRMSE = {{\sqrt {{{\sum\nolimits_{t = 1}^n {{{({\mathtilde{y}_t} - y)}^2}} } \over n}} } \over {{y_{t\_\max}} - {y_{t\_\min}}}} \times 100\% \eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">NRMSE = {{\sqrt {{{\sum\nolimits_{t = 1}^n {{{({\mathtilde{y}_t} - y)}^2}} } \over n}} } \over {{y_{t\_\max}} - {y_{t\_\min}}}} \times 100\% \eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathtilde{y}_t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{\mathtilde{y}_t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the value sequence of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at Latin hypercube sampling points in vector space <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vec x = (a, d, w, b, s)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">\vec x = (a, d, w, b, s)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> defining an antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value for an optimum <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vec x</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">\vec x</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">n</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the number of samples to be evaluated, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{y_{t\_\max}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">{y_{t\_\max}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{y_{t\_\min}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">{y_{t\_\min}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are the maximum and minimum values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> among <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathtilde{y}_t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">{\mathtilde{y}_t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. A smaller <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value indicates a better tolerance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-fold slot antenna to fabrication errors.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Tag Design and Fabrication Errors Analysis</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Antenna Parameters Optimization</h3><p>In the design simulation, thickness of the aluminum foil is set to be 0.025 mm, and thickness of the plastic substrate of blister is 0.5 mm. Typical blister plastic is polyvinyl chloride, which has a dielectric constant of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\varepsilon _{\rm r}} = 3.19</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">{\varepsilon _{\rm r}} = 3.19</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and dielectric loss of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\tan\delta } = 0.0096</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">{\tan\delta } = 0.0096</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>For demonstration, we consider Impinj Monza-4 chip for the RFID tag, which has an input impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{Z_C} = 11 - 143j(\Omega)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">{Z_C} = 11 - 143j(\Omega)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at UHF 915 MHz <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3a">[16]</a>.</p><p>For an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-fold slot antenna structure defined in restricted design space <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm L}3 \times {\rm L}4 = 40 \times 8~\hbox{mm}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">{\rm L}3 \times {\rm L}4 = 40 \times 8~\hbox{mm}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on aluminum foil of dimensions <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm L}1 \times {\rm L}2 = 46 \times 92~\hbox{mm}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">{\rm L}1 \times {\rm L}2 = 46 \times 92~\hbox{mm}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, we may optimize its structure parameters by numerical simulation design. All the simulations were performed with the whole blister package, viz., a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">46 \times 92\hbox{-mm}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">46 \times 92\hbox{-mm}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> aluminum foil attached to a plastic sheet with air-filled slot in the aluminum foil as antenna. In the optimization, sequential nonlinear programming method <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_3a">[17]</a> is applied. Maximum normalized tag performance index in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> is used as a prior optimization objective, and small as possible <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value serves as another design objective.</p><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> lists the optimized structure parameters for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for slots of different fold numbers. From <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>, we find that the RFID tag with one-fold slot antenna provides the largest <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value, while the tag with zero-fold slot antenna has the smallest <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value. Slot antennas of more than two folds (viz., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m \geq 2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">m \geq 2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) have even larger <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values but similar <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values, so that they do not provide considerable merit.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Antenna parameters for tag performance index <span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau}</script> and <span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">NRMSE</script><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>Both the slot antennas for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">m = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and 1 have dipole-like radiation patterns. Tag with zero-fold slot antenna has a gain of around 0 dBi, and tag with one-fold slot antenna has a gain of 0.8372 dBi.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Effects of Fabrication Errors</h3><p>For the designed tag antennas given in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>, we may analyze the effects of fabrication errors for verification by taking 500 Latin hypercube sampling points to simulate the fabrication process. Probability distributions of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value based on Latin hypercube sampling are presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Probability distribution of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value based on Latin hypercube sampling. (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{m}=0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">{m}=0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{m}=1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">{m}=1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (c) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{m}=2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">{m}=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (d) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{m}=3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">{m}=3</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7286772/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>, the dotted lines indicate expected <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value obtained from optimized parameters shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. The range of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values of all the 500 sampling points is divided into 50 intervals, and the probability of them appearing in a certain interval can be read from the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">x</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">x</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis. Values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3" href="#deqn3" class="fulltext-link">(3)</a> of the 500 sampling points for tag of slot antenna of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">m = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">m = 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">m = 2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">m = 3</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are 17.80%, 43.12%, 47.07%, and 68.44%, respectively.</p><p>From the probability distributions in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a>, it is found that 67.6% of the samples for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">m = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> have <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values within a dynamic range of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">0.2010\pm 0.1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">0.2010\pm 0.1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which leads to the smallest <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value. Therefore, the zero-fold slot antenna suffers less from the fabrication errors than any other slot antennas.</p><p>Although tags for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">m = 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, 2, and 3 have satisfactory <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values, they have large <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> so that suffer more from the fabrication errors. From the probability distributions in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b), (c) and (d)</a>, it is found that 4.0% of the samples for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">m = 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> have <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values less than 0.1, while 21.4% of the samples for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">m = 2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and 62.4% of the samples for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 3</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">m = 3</script></tex-math></inline-formula> have <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">\sqrt {{G_r}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values less than 0.1. Therefore, tags for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m \geq 2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">m \geq 2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are not practical because of the hazard of tag performance degradation.</p><p>Comparison between <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a) and (b)</a> indicates that roughly 96% of samples for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = 1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">m = 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> have <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-97">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values larger than the expected <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }=0.2010</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }=0.2010</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for samples of zero-fold slot, although tags with one-fold slot may suffer more from the fabrication errors than tags with zero-fold slot.</p><p>Therefore, judging from both the tag performance and tolerance to fabrication errors, RFID tag with one-fold slot is highly recommended for medicine blister package although RFID tag with zero-fold slot has a more stable performance.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Experiment Test</h2></div><p>For demonstration, tags with the designed zero-fold and one-fold slot antenna are fabricated and tested in the laboratory.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> shows two prototypes of medicine blister package with RFID tag integrated into aluminum foil with zero-fold and one-fold slot antenna, respectively. The aluminum foil has a plastic substrate of thickness of 0.5 mm. Both the prototypes are made with fabrication errors at the general level of hot-press for aluminum blister medicine packaging.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Prototype medicine blister with UHF RFID tags integrated into aluminum foil. (a) zero-fold slot. (b) one-fold slot.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7286772/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The prototypes have been tested by using an Alien ALR-9900 RFID reader, which has an EIRP of 4 W. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 5</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6</a> show the typical normalized patterns in measured read range for prototype tags with zero-fold antenna and one-fold antenna, respectively. For comparison, the calculated read range patterns obtained from the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">\sqrt {{G_{\rm r}}\tau }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> value shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> are also presented. We have the observation that the measured and calculated patterns are in good agreement.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Normalized read-range pattern of the zero-fold UHF tag on aluminum foil. (a) pattern in E-plane. (b) pattern in H-plane.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7286772/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Normalized read-range pattern of the one-fold UHF tag on aluminum foil. (a) pattern in E-plane. (b) pattern in H-plane.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7286772/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The statistics of measured maximum read range of 50 sample tags with zero-fold slot and one-fold slot are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a) and (b)</a>, respectively. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> is presented by scaling the maximum read range with step of 0.5 m and recording the number of sample tags that can be interrogated at different read ranges. It is observed that distributions of maximum read range in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a) and (b)</a> agree well with the analytical probability distributions shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a) and (b)</a>, respectively.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7286772/7286772-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Statistical measurement of 50 samples. (a) tags with zero-fold slot. (b) tags with one-fold slot.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7286772/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The statistics indicate an average maximum read range of 1.18 m for tags with zero-fold slot and 3.19 m for tags with one-fold slot. Therefore, with general fabrication errors under the same hot-press fabrication process, RFID tags with one-fold slot antenna provide preferable read range.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In order to integrate passive UHF RFID tag into medicine blister package with aluminum foil, the UHF tag antenna must be strictly restricted within a small design space, and effects of fabrication errors in hot-press fabrication of medicine aluminum blister should be considered.</p><p>Slot antenna is proved to be a satisfactory tag antenna for medicine blister. However, fabrication errors in hot-press fabrication of medicine blister exclude the use of multifold slot antenna although a tag with multifold slot antenna tends to have a large read range. Analysis based on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">NRMSE</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">NRMSE</script></tex-math></inline-formula> indicates that RFID tag with zero-fold has the best tolerance to hot-press fabrication error. Judging from both the maximum read range and tolerance to fabrication errors, RFID tag with one-slot antenna deserves the highest recommendation.</p><p>In addition, we find that shape of aluminum blister and medicine types in blisters have little effect on the tag's radiation pattern and read range. By pressing the prototypes in different ways, it is measured that the maximum read range may be decreased by approximately 13% for tag of one-fold slot and 3% for tag of zero-fold slot. The tag with one-fold slot antenna still has read range larger than that of a tag with zero-fold slot.</p></div>
</div></div>
</div><!-- end ngIf: ft.sectionText -->

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
